Welcome to the world of sportscars

Overview

The debut of the Le Mans Prototype in 1999 marked the start of the modern era of sportscar racing, with the new cars being able to race not only at the 24h of Le Mans, but also in a new championship series in America using the same regulations from the ACO. Further series in Europe and Asia were initially planned and some became reality, leading to the creation of the FIA World Endurance Championship in 2012. This led to the demise of the top class in America, but after the creation of the Le Mans Hypercar in 2021 and LMDh in 2023 the top class of sportscar racing is again shared across championships both in Europe and America.

Before 1999

As Group C died out in the Early 90s, leading to the end of the World Sportscar Championship at the end of 1992, and the GTP class being replaced in the IMSA GT championship after 1993, the top class increasingly consisted of smaller, slower open-cockpit prototypes with production based engines, called the World Sports Car (WSC). These were only moderately successful, leading ACO to open up the top class at Le Mans both to older Group C cars, but also allowing GT cars to be able to fight for the overall win as part of the new LMGT1 class. In 1995 the top class became available only to WSC-cars, but the LMGT1 regulations were kept the same. What manufacturers realised was that the GT1 regulations were so open that they could basically built a bespoke prototype and only built 1 road-going version to be able to race. this was first exploited in 1994 when Dauer modified a Porsche 962C and created 1 roadcar, allowing them to take the overall win with the Dauer 962. McLaren teamed up with BMW to create the McLaren F1 GTR, to take their overall win in 1995. While Porsche, together with TWR and Joest Racing won with a WSC car in 1996 and 1997, Several new manufacturers built new GT1 cars specifically for that race. Porsche Entered the 911 GT1 in 1996, Nissan and Panoz debuted the R391 GT1 and GTR-1 in 1997, and in 1998 Toyota joined with their purpose-built GT-One together with Mercedes with the CLK-LM. At this point the open nature of the regulations were becoming ridiculous, with manufacturers building cars specifically for this class because they only needed to produce a single road-going model. The regulations specified since these were supposed to be GT cars, that they needed boot space capable of holding a standard size suitcase. Mercedes had placed this space underneath the rear bodywork in a very impractical place. Meanwhile, Toyota managed to convince the scrutineers that because the fuel tank of the GT-One was empty during scrutineering, it could theoretically fit the required space. The by now complete disregard for the intention of the regulations, combined with Mercedes wiping the field clean in the newly created FIA GT Championship to the extent that nobody else entered the class in 1999, the FIA were forced to drop the class for that year. This forced the ACO to rethink the class structure at Le Mans, leading to the creation of the Le Mans Prototype (LMP) and the Le Mans Grand Touring Prototype (LMGTP). Cars in the old LMGT1 class could be modified to fit in the LMGTP class for closed cockpit prototypes, while the LMP class was for open cockpit cars. The GT1 class was dropped, with the former GT2 class being renamed GTS as the top GT class, with GT3-spec cars being eligible in the new GT class. With the introduction of these new cars, the ACO looked for opportunities to create a championship with Le Mans-style regulations. They struck an Agreement with IMSA to replace the IMSA GT Championship with the new American Le Mans Series starting in 1999 after testing the format in the penultimate round of the 1998 IMSA GT Championship, which became the first running of the Petit Le Mans. The IMSA GT Championship had just lost two of its key events to the newly revived US Road Racing Championship, which soon after became the Rolex Sports Car Series. The split caused the two series to be direct competitors, IMSA with their ageing WSC prototypes, and the USRRC creating their own prototype class together with the International Sports Racing Series in Europe. IMSA saw the opportunity to partner with the ACO and create the ALMS with the new LMP's making up the top class. For ACO this was just the start, and they were planning similar championships in Europe and Asia as well.



1999 Season

Overview:

The demise of the LMGT1 class led Toyota and Mercedes to adapt their GT-One and CLK-LM to fit in the LMGTP class, the Mercedes becoming the CLR. Nissan chose to modify the R390 to become the open-cockpit R391 LMP. Porsche started work on a new car, the LMP2000, but discussions over which engine to use delayed the project to 2000, and then it was cancelled in the spring of 1999 due to internal politics. BMW modified their V12 LM from 1998 built for the WSC-spec top class into the V12 LMR to race in the new LMP class. Audi joined the sportscar scene with two newly developed cars, the R8R for the LMP class, and the R8C for the LMGTP class. The R8R was designed and built by Dallara in Italy, whereas the R8C was designed by Racing Technology Norfolk in the UK. Both programs were operated by Joest Racing. Panoz also designed the new LMP-1 Roadster-S, a front-engined open-cockpit LMP. BMW debuted the V12 LMR at the first round of the ALMS at Sebring, and they were joined by Audi with their R8R. Whereas Audi only did Sebring before focusing on Le Mans, BMW ran a partial season, only skipping the second round between Sebring and Le Mans. The new Panoz joined the ALMS at the second round and completed the season in addition to Le Mans. Toyota, Mercedes and Nissan focused only on Le Mans. As part of the process of expanding sportscar racing across the world, the ACO planned a non-championship Le Mans-style race in Japan to gauge the interest in Asia for an ALMS-type series. Toyota and Nissan both sent a car each to the race in addition to competing at Le Mans.

The remaining #6 was then withdrawn
    Toyota were the favourites to win, but the team struggled with explosive punctures, #1 retiring on Saturday evening, and the #2 crashing out heavily during the night. The #3 was catching the leader towards the end of the race, but suffered another puncture in the last hour, ending the race in 2nd
    BMW didn't have the fastest car, but they took the lead by having to pit less often for fuel, and having fewer mechanical issues. #17 was on couse to win but crashed out on Sunday with just a few hours to go, handing the lead and the win to the #15
    Nissan and Panoz struggled with reliability, while Audi didn't have the ultimate pace, but good reliability meant the two R8Rs finished 3rd and 4th

Season Totals:

Number of Races: 10
Total Distance Covered: 12177.746 km



2000 Season

Overview:

After the scary accidents suffered by the Mercedes' at Le Mans was found to be because of a fundamental aerodynamic instability of the car, the team withdrew from racing and the CLRs never raced again. Nissan and Toyota both also withdrew from sportscars at the end of the year, with Toyota planning to enter F1. BMW Entered F1 in 2000, thus ending their international sportscar program, but they continued racing with Schnitzer for the full season of ALMS. They were joined by Audi debuting their new R8 after getting up to speed in 1999. Cadillac joined with the new Northstar LMP, testing it in both the ALMS and the GARRC, however it was proving uncompetitive.
ACO again restructured the classes for Le Mans, renaming the previous year's LMP class LMP900, and adding the LMP675-class for smaller, lighter prototypes. The prototypes running in the GARRC and the FIA Sportscar Championship could be modified to run in either class. The 900/675-designation refers to the minimum weight of the cars, 900 kg for the top class, 675 kg for the other.
ALMS expanded the calendar for 2000, including 2 rounds in Europe to help launch the ELMS for 2001, as well as the final round in Australia to launch the APLMS a year later.

Season Totals:

Number of Races: 13
Total Distance Covered: 14064.568 km



2001 Season

Overview:

After not making the trip to Australia with their prototypes, BMW retired their V12 LMRs, and for 2001 they competed in the GT class with the new V8-powered M3 GTR. Audi continued racing in ALMS alongside Le Mans with two factory cars, in addition they also sold customer cars to Champion Racing in ALMS and Johansson Motorsport in ELMS. Panoz debuted the LMP07, but after suffering big problems with reliability in the first part of the season they chose to abandon the new car and brought back the old cars. Bentley debuted the closed-cockpit EXP Speed 8 at Le Mans, reviving the LMGTP class which had no entrants in 2000. The dominant Dodge Vipers were retired from the GTS class as Chrysler started developement of a brand new LMP-car together with Oreca. The new car debuted at the Donington ELMS-race.
After debuting at Le Mans in 2000, ALMS took on the LMP900 and LMP675 classes as well in place of the general LMP-class used in 1999 and 2000. ELMS also ran the same 4 classes.
After the ALMS staged two races in Europe in 2000, ALMS organizer Professional Sports Car Racing was looking to expand and the ELMS was launched as a sister series in Europe, with four races shared between the two series, which were optional for the teams. Sebring and Petit Le Mans were optional for the European teams, while the events at Donington Park and Jarama were optional for the American teams. Due to a lack of interest from teams, the ELMS only lasted one season and was not continued for 2002. The ELMS ended up competing against series like FIA Sportscar Championship and FIA GT Championship which used similar cars, but they had to be modified to race in ELMS. This meant few teams were interested in racing in ELMS due to the resources necessary and impracticality of competing across the different series. The APLMS were also scheduled to start in the autums with events at Sepang and Adelaide, but these were cancelled for various reasons, and although the series was set to go ahead in 2002, it was abandoned due to a lack of interest.
Plans were announced in September 1999 to build a new race track in Aruba. The organizer had an agreement to host the ALMS season opener in 2001, however the 4.345 km Aruba International Raceway was never built due to a conflict between the track promoter and the Aruban government over funding and the event was never officially on the 2001 calendar. The failure to comply with the agreements made with ALMS and other series it was supposed to host the organizer ended up mired in legal cases, which the Aruban government eventually lost after shutting down the plans.

Season Totals:

Number of Races: 14
Total Distance Covered: 13497.302 km



2002 Season

Overview:

Audi and Panoz continued their programs in ALMS, with Panoz debuting the LMP01 Evo, an updated version of the LMP-1 Roadster-S following the previous year's flawed LMP07. Panoz' and Audis also competed in the hands of privateer teams, Audi with Champion Racing, and Panoz with several teams, of note MBD who used the discarded LMP07s fitted with Mugen engines. Cadillac continued their program racing at Le Mans as well as a partial ALMS season, debuting their new Northstar LMP02 with an all new chassis, and it was proving increasingly competititive towards the end of the season. Bentley continued racing at Le Mans with the EXP Speed 8 whilst developing a new car for 2003.
BMW meanwhile announced in January the cancellation of its ALMS GT program with the M3 GTR after rule changes for the LMGT category limiting its competitiveness of the controversial V8 engine.
Ferrari debuted a new car in the GTS class, the 550 Maranello, which was developed in parallel by Team Rafanelli in Italy and Prodrive in the UK. The car initially proved uncompetitive, but after switching from a 5.5L to a 6.0L V12 engine, it started challenging the Corvettes.
At the end of 2001 the ALMS organizer changed its name from Professional Sports Car Racing to bring back the famous IMSA name it had held previously, until a change of ownership in 1997.
After completing the final races of the ELMS in 2001 with as few as 14 cars on the grid, the 2002 season was cancelled in december citing the lack of entrants and the unstable nature of the world following the events of 11th of September.
The ALMS announced an expanded calendar, with new events at Road America, Washington D.C., Trois-Rivieres and Miami, and a move away from rovals that had been on the calendar in the previous years. The calendar was initially announced with longer races, with all races being at least 3-4 hours long, however most events were reverted back to the normal 2h 45min format after input from TV broadcasters. Following the failure of the ELMS in Europe, ALMS returned to only hosting races inside North America.
With the planned debut of the APLMS in 2001 hitting trouble with both its first two rounds cancelled for various reasons, the series were abandoned with the Malaysia event becoming an invitational event.

Season Totals:

Number of Races: 11
Total Distance Covered: 12252,745 km



2003 Season

Overview:

Audi pulled out of sportscar racing after 2002 as a works team, however the cars kept racing for privateer teams. Joest Racing and Champion Racing contested ALMS, With Champion Racing joining Audi Sport Team UK and the Japanese Team Goh at Le Mans.
Panoz also pulled out as a factory team, with its two LMP01s racing under the JML Team Panoz banner in both ALMS and Le Mans, however the ageing cars struggled for pace.
Bentley debuted a new car, the Speed 8, contesting the 12h of Sebring for the first time as well as Le Mans. Tom Kristensen and Dindo Capello jumped ship from Audi to join the team.
After its most successful year of the program, Cadillac elected not to extend the project, and did not return to sportscar racing in 2003.
In the GT class, Ferrari debuted with the 360 Modena GTC, initially struggeling to be competitive against the armada of Porsches, though getting faster with more developement by the time 2004 started.
ALMS revealed the new calendar for 2003 with a new race in Mexico City, as well as a planned race in Europe in May. However the European race was soon abandoned after a suitable venue couldn't be agreed on. The format of the Road America race was also changed from 500 Miles to the standard 2h 45min.
Meanwhile, two years on from the failed ELMS, ACO tried again to plan its own sportscar championship in Europe. To prepare for this, it set up another experimental race at La Sarthe to check the interest before committing to the new LMES in 2004.

Season Totals:

Number of Races: 11
Total Distance Covered: 12880.997 km



2004 Season

Overview:

Audi started work on a new car to succeed the R8, which would ultimately debut in 2006. Meanwhile the Joest Team ended their program in ALMS, leaving only Champion Racing competing in the US. In Europe, Team Goh and Audi Sport UK also operated Audis in the new LMES, with Team UK also making the trip to Sebring.
After winning Le Mans in the 3rd year of the program, Bentley ended their sportscar program and didn't return. Panoz too elected not to return in the top class with the LMP01, instead focusing on their GT-class program.
With the new LMP1 regulations, the Reynard 02S project was revived, originally developed in 2002 before the company went bankrupt, the design was taken over by International Racing Management and renamed the DBA 03S. As Zytek was being tasked with building more of these chassis, they were also badged as the Zytek 04S. The cars were run by several teams and they were proving to have good pace but struggled with reliability.
In the GTS class, Ferrari debuted the 575 Maranello, an evolution of the 550 at Sebring as well as the full LMES season. Lamborghini also joined the class in ALMS at Mid-Ohio with the Murcielago R-GT, however the car struggled for pace and reliability.
ACO announced changes in the class structure, with LMP900 and LMP675 being replaced by LMP1 and LMP2. LMP900 and LMGTP-cars moved to LMP1, and LMP675 cars could be converted to either of the new classes. Rule changes were also announced for LMP1 with overhang limited and the floor structure changed to limit downforce and make the cars less likely to take off. IMSA announced that they would delay enforcing these new rules in ALMS, allowing both new LMP1 and LMP2 cars and old LMP900 and LMP675 cars to compete in what became the P1 and P2 class. This allowed Dyson racing to continue using their LMP675 MG-Lolas, moving them into the P1 class.
ALMS announced their new calendar for 2004, with a focus on making sure all events could be run following cancellations and replacements in the last few years. The calendar included a return to Mid-Ohio and Portland, as well as a new event at Lime Rock Park. Laguna Seca also became the season finale, with the race extended to 4 hours.
After the Announcement of the 1000 km of Le Mans preview race in 2003, ACO launched the new Le Mans Endurance Series, with 4 1000km events across Europe. Having learned from the ELMS in 2001, the new series attracted several teams from the FIA Sportscar championship and FIA GT championship, forcing the end of those series.

Season Totals:

Number of Races: 14
Total Distance Covered: 16229.946 km



2005 Season

Overview:

With the ageing Audi R8 still being competitive, the ACO announced that 2005 would be the last year that cars built to the old LMP900 rules would be permitted to race, and the cars were also handicapped with more ballast and less power than the newer LMP1 machines. Older generation LMP900 cars would still be allowed to race in ALMS, with IMSA not enforcing the new rules yet, allowing older cars to compete alongside newer LMP1 cars.
The FIA and ACO also revised the classes for GT-cars, with LMGTS and LMGT replaced by LMGT1 and LMGT2. The new classes were designed to more tightly control and balance the cars, with specific laptime requirements set. The new structure meant new cars would have to be homologated by the FIA before being allowed to compete.
In the US, Champion Racing continued racing their two R8s, also competing at Le Mans. Audi Sport Team UK and Team Goh chose not to continue beyond 2004, with Team Oreca taking over one of the R8s to compete in the LMES and Le Mans.
In Europe, a new challenger to the Audis Emerged in the form of Pescarolo. After several years of developing their Courage-designed C60, and after switching from Peugeot to a Judd V10 engine, the Pescarolo C60 Hybrid was proving fast enough to take on Audi, with the team completing the LMES season and Le Mans with a pair of cars.
In the GT-classes, new cars were introduced with the new regulations. Corvette replaced the old C5-R with the new C6.R, and Aston Martin joined with the brand new DBR9. There was also controversy as IMSA allowed Maserati to run in the GT1 clas in ALMS with the MC12, despite the car not being built to LMGT1 spec. The decision drew criticism from ACO and from several of the teams, with Aston Martin protesting the car at the first round in Sebring. Meanwhile Lamborghini didn't continue into 2005 with the Krohn-Barbour team not feeling the necessary factory support to make the cars competitive.
The schedule for the 24h of Le Mans was adjusted after discussions between IMSA and the ACO who were finding it challenging to schedule races early in the season with the mandatory test day being a month before the race forcing both ALMS and LMES to effectively take a long break to allow teams to race at Le Mans. In 2005 the test day was moved to 2 weeks before the race, allowing more flexibility for ALMS to schedule more races early in the season.
IMSA focused on concistency in the ALMS calendar, keeping all events from 2004 as well as adding the return of a sprint event at Road Atlanta. they also took advantage of the Le Mans test day being moved to reschedule Mid-Ohio to May, before Le Mans.
LMES also focused on steady growth after a successful first season, keeping the 4 events from 2004, and adding a fifth round at the new Istanbul Park.

    This meant the #3 Champion Audi could control the pace after a flawless run to take the win, with Tom Kristensen taking a record-breaking 7th Le Mans win

Season Totals:

Number of Races: 16
Total Distance Covered: 17184.822 km



2006 Season

Overview:

With the ACO outlawing old LMP900 cars from Le Mans, Audi revealed the R10 TDI to replace the R8. That also coincided with Audi returning as a factory team, cooperating with Champion Racing in ALMS with team Joest running the cars at Le Mans. With IMSA still allowing older cars to compete, it also gave them the opportunity to take a single R8 on a farewell tour over the first few ALMS rounds while the R10s were testing for Le Mans. News also came in 2005 that Peugeot would also join LMP1 in 2007 with their own diesel-powered prototype.
After debuting in the ALMS season finale in 2005, Porsche launched into the first full season with its Penske-run LMP2 car. The team was however not allowed to race at Le Mans, due to the ACO not allowing factory teams in the LMP2 class. Pescarolo continued racing in Europe with its C60 Hybrid, after a successful 2005-season.
ALMS released a new calendar, with Sonoma and the spring race at Road Atlanta being replaced by a race at the new Miller Motorsports Park in Utah, and a new street circuit in Houston Texas, run together with Champ Car.
LMES continued with a 5-race calendar with a few shuffled dates, as well as switching the British round from Silverstone to Donington Park. The series also underwent a slight rebranding, and became known simply as the Le Mans Series.
Work conducted by the people behind Team Goh culminated in the debut of the new ACO-backed Japan Le Mans Challenge, organizing 3 1000 km races in Japan, in an effort to get japanese teams interested in international sportscar racing.

    The race quickly became a stranglehold by the Audis, having more pace and better fuel economy than the Pescarolos.
    Problems started during the 3rd hour for the leading #7 Audi, first having to make an extra pit stop after rubber dislodged the windscreen, and an hour later it was in the garage to replace the fuel injectors, which dropped it down the order
    The two Pescarolos also suffered issues in the early night hours, #16 had a lengthy stay in the garage trying to fix some electrical issues, and #17 went off and got stuck in the gravel
    #7 Audi was back in the garage approaching 9h in after suffering contact breaking a wishbone, and after rejoining briefly it came back to the garage with floor damage
    #8 Audi had a comfortable lead, but nearing the half way point there was drama as it was wheeled into the garage with gearbox issues, however it managed to exit the pits still leading. It soon had to pit again with a slow puncture, but the time loss was minimal
    As Sunday morning dawned the leading #8 had another scare, with a marshal stopping it at the end of the pit lane, forcing it to be rolled back to the pit box after one of the headlamps had failed. Shortly afterwards #7 slowed on track again, spending yet more time in the garage with a broken turbocharger
    During the rest of Sunday the cars ran reliably, with #8 cruising home to take the win ahead of the #17 Pescarolo and the recovering #7 Audi

Season Totals:

Number of Races: 16
Total Distance Covered: 17202.127 km



2007 Season

Overview:

The big news of the season was Peugeot returning to sportscar racing with the 908 HDi FAP, competing in the Le Mans Series. Audi continued their program in the ALMS, joined by Porsche who revealed an upgraded evolution of the RS Spyder, however Porsche continuing to focus exclusively on ALMS. The new car was also run by Dyson racing, who replaced the Lolas from 2006, moving down to the P2 class.
Acura joined ALMS with a new factory effort in the P2 class. For the first season they took a Courage LC75 chassis and upgraded it extensively, badging the car as the ARX-01a in the P2 class at Sebring. Two of the teams ran the new car, with the 3rd factory-supported team racing a Lola chassis, focusing purely on engine developement.
A big talking point was the lack of pace difference between the P1 and P2 cars in the ALMS, with IMSA deciding not to follow the ACO in reducing the restrictor diameter by 5% for LMP2 cars, allowing them to be much closer to the P1 Audis on pace.
After winning every LMS race of the season, Pescarolo switched their focus to building a new car themselves, debuting the new Pescarolo 01 at the LMS opener at Monza. The car was able to run in both LMP1 and LMP2 depending on the engine specification, with several teams running it as customer cars.
ALMS revealed a revised calendar with 3 new events, racing at street circuits in St. Petersburg and Detroit together with the IRL, and joining Champ Car at Long Beach. The new calendar also saw the event at Road America extended to 4 hours, and the Portland race dropped off the calendar.
The LMS also revealed a modified calendar, returning to Monza and Silverstone, as well as a new event in Valencia in Spain. A 6th event was added later in the form of Interlagos in Brazil, running to 1000 Miles rather than the usual 1000 km distance. The event in Istanbul dropped off the calendar after two years.
After a slow start in 2006, the JLMC planned a steady growth by keeping the 3 races from 2006, and adding a 4th race at Fuji. The hope was that the 2007 season would see more notable entrants and bigger grids compared to the previous season.

  1. Mobil 1 12 Hours of Sebring
    Sebring International Raceway, Sebring, Florida
    Date: 17.03.2007
    Series: ALMS
    Race Format: 12 Hours
    Classes: P1, P2, GT1, GT2
    Circuit Length: 6.019 km
    Laps Completed: 364
    Distance Covered: 2190.916 km
    Number of cars entered: 34 (4 P1, 9 P2, 3 GT1, 18 GT2)
    Number of cars finished: 24 (3 P1, 7 P2, 3 GT1, 11 GT2)
    Pole Position: #2 Audi Sport North America, Audi R10 TDI, Frank Biela(DEU), Emanuele Pirro(ITA), Marco Werner(DEU), 1.44,974
    Overall Winner: #2 Audi Sport North America, Audi R10 TDI, Frank Biela(DEU), Emanuele Pirro(ITA), Marco Werner(DEU), 12:01.14,838
    P2 Winner: #26 Andretti Green Racing, Acura ARX-01a, Bryan Herta(USA), Dario Franchitti(GBR), Tony Kanaan(BRA), +6 Laps
    GT1 Winner: #4 Corvette Racing, Chevrolet Corvette C6.R, Oliver Gavin(GBR), Olivier Beretta(MCO), Max Papis(ITA), +23 Laps
    GT2 Winner: #62 Risi Competizione, Ferrari F430 GTC, Mika Salo(FIN), Johnny Mowlem(GBR), Jaime Melo(BRA), +34 Laps
    The two Audis led the early laps ahead of #7 Porsche, with #1 taking the lead 15 min in as #2 hit traffic. #6 Porsche suffered brake issues in the first hour and dropped down the order. As the Audis made their first stop #2 was penalized for a pit stop infringement, and then in the 2nd hour suffered a puncture costing it 2 laps limping back to the pits, it was then penalized an hour later for speeding in the pit lane, with #1 was also penalized shortly after for contact in the pit lane with #16 Dyson. That left #7 Porsche in the lead, but it soon pitted with electrical issues, the team initially changing the battery, but the car lost a lot of time in the pits repeatedly for more new batteries and eventually a new alternator cable. #6 Porsche also suffered similar electrical issues and it too dropped a long way down with repeated visits to the pits. #1 Audi pitted for a routine stop at the 5h mark, but failed to start and the car dropped down the order, suffering the same issue multiple times over the following few hours. That left #2 back in the lead after its earlier problems, with the new #26 Acura 2nd overall and #9 Acura 3rd, until #9 slowed with electrical issues, it too dropping down the order. #2 made a routine stop approaching 7h, but was penalized for a pit stop infringement and held for an extra 40s. Following a series of safety cars #26 ended up right behind the leading #2, but over the final few hours it drifted to 6 laps down with multiple stops for small repairs as well as clearing the radiators and refilling gearbox oil, while #2 Audi cruised home to take the win

    Overall Winner: #1 Audi Sport North America, Audi R10 TDI, Frank Biela(DEU), Emanuele Pirro(ITA), Marco Werner(DEU), 24:02.42,628

Drama in the 2nd hour as #3 Audi crashed out, retiring on the spot and causing a lengthy safety car to repair the barrier. With just 3h to go #7 Peugeot suffered engine issues, and after trying to repair it in the garage, it too retired from the race. Rain started falling with 2 hours to go, forcing everyone to switch to wets, and as the rain intensified the safety car was deployed in the final hour, with #8 Peugeot being rolled into the garage with a gearbox issue. 10 minutes from the end the safety car pulled in, but #1 Audi comfortably cruised home to take the win, with #8 Peugeot finishing 2nd after stopping and waiting for the finish

    Distance Covered: 1001.572 km

    Pole Position: #7 Team Peugeot Total, Peugeot 908 HDi FAP, Nicolas Minassian(FRA), Marc Gene(ESP), 2.00,105
    Overall Winner: #8 Team Peugeot Total, Peugeot 908 HDi FAP, Stephane Sarrazin(FRA), Pedro Lamy(POR), 5:47.47,313

    Peugeot again locked out the front row and controlled the opening stages, with #7 ahead until #8 took the lead a few laps in. #8 Peugeot maintained the lead through the first cycle of pit stops, but #7 pitted again just before the hour mark and went into the garage with a wheel bearing issue. After initially rejoining several laps down #7 went back in the garage and retired before the end of the 2nd hour. A brief rainshower in the 4th hour made conditions difficult, but the leaders stayed out on slicks. #8 maintained the lead through a myriad of safety cars to take the win, with the two factory Pescarolos ending up 2nd and 4th, either side of the LMP2 winner

  14. Grand Prix of Mosport
    Mosport International Raceway, Bowmanville, Ontario
    Date: 26.08.2007
    Series: ALMS
    Race Format: 2 Hours 45 minutes
    Classes: P1, P2, GT1, GT2
    Circuit Length: 3.957 km
    Laps Completed: 125
    Distance Covered: 494.625 km
    Number of cars entered: 25 (4 P1, 9 P2, 3 GT1, 9 GT2)
    Number of cars finished: 21 (3 P1, 7 P2, 3 GT1, 8 GT2)
    Pole Position: #1 Audi Sport North America, Audi R10 TDI, Rinaldo Capello(ITA), Allan McNish(GBR), 1.05,829
    Overall Winner: #7 Penske Motorsports, Porsche RS Spyder Evo, Timo Bernhard(DEU), Romain Dumas(FRA), 2:45.43,043

    #1 Audi Started on pole ahead of #7 Porsche, but #2 Audi took 2nd at the start, with the Audis leading the opening stages, as #26 Acura split the Porsches. The Audis made their first stop just before the hour mark, before a safety car period triggered by #9 Acura going off after contact. The Porsches made their first stop under the safety car, with the two Audis making a 2nd stop a lap later. However major confusion in the pit lane saw #2 Audi penalized and dropped a lap down, with #1 ending up 3rd overall. On the restart #1 Audi quickly re-took the lead and started to pull away. As the leaders made their last stop #1 maintained its lead as #6 Porsche suffered a puncture and had to pit again. #1 Audi had built a comfortable lead and was set to take the win until a gearbox issue started costing it time and eventually #7 Porsche breezed past with less than 10 min to go to take the win, with #1 ending up 2nd after fending off #6 Porsche in the closing laps as the issue became progressively worse

    Circuit Length: 3.331 km

    Distance Covered: 353.086 km
    Number of cars entered: 26 (4 P1, 8 P2, 2 GT1, 12 GT2)
    Number of cars finished: 19 (3 P1, 8 P2, 2 GT1, 6 GT2)
    Pole Position: #6 Penske Motorsports, Porsche RS Spyder Evo, Sascha Maassen(DEU), Ryan Briscoe(AUS), 1.13,357
    Overall Winner: #7 Penske Motorsports, Porsche RS Spyder Evo, Timo Bernhard(DEU), Romain Dumas(FRA), 2:45.36,179

    The Porsches locked out the front row and led the start ahead of #26 Acura, however the Audis were bouncing back from a bad qualifying with #1 taking 3rd. Drama as the leading #6 Porsche got tangled up in traffic and spun, handing it a stop/go penalty and the lead to #7. The leaders made their first stop during an early safety car, #7 maintaining the net lead as other cars stayed out to get track position. #1 Audi took over the net lead on the restart, as #6 Porsche moved into the overall lead and #2 Audi was dealt a stop/go for contact. #26 Acura slowed with electrical issues near the hour mark, dropping many laps down trying to fix the issue. #6 Porsche eventually pitted for its first stop 1h 15min in, with the safety car coming out shortly after. That allowed #7 Porsche and the 2 Audis to make their 2nd stop, #7 cycling to the lead. #2 Audi made a blinding launch at the restart to jump straight to the overall lead, as #9 Acura spun and made contact with #6 Porsche, which suffered a damaged rear wing. #2 Audi controlled the lead, but after heavy pressure from #7 Porsche in the closing stages the Audi cracked and #7 muscled its way past to take the win in the final minutes

    Date: 06.10.2007

    Circuit Length: 4.088 km

    Distance Covered: 1610.672 km
    Number of cars entered: 31 (7 P1, 9 P2, 3 GT1, 12 GT2)
    Number of cars finished: 19 (5 P1, 6 P2, 1 GT1, 7 GT2)
    Pole Position: #2 Audi Sport North America, Audi R10 TDI, Emanuele Pirro(ITA), Marco Werner(DEU), Lucas Luhr(DEU), 1.08,906
    Overall Winner: #1 Audi Sport North America, Audi R10 TDI, Rinaldo Capello(ITA), Allan McNish(GBR), 9:18.58,275
    P2 Winner: #7 Penske Motorsports, Porsche RS Spyder Evo, Timo Bernhard(DEU), Romain Dumas(FRA), Patrick Long(USA), +0,923

After fighting back to lie 2nd overall #2 Audi was involved in an incident in the 3rd hour sending it off the road, the car managed to get back to the pits but dropped many laps repairing the damage. #1 Audi also suffered damage after ending up involved in an incident ahead, forcing it too into the pits briefly for repairs. As the race was nearing 6h #9 Acura pitted during a lengthy safety car to fix a starter motor problem that had plagued the car throughout the race. #6 Porsche had a steady race until the 7th hour, when multiple stops to fix damage sustained in a 2nd hour incident dropped it down the order. In the closing hours #1 Audi briefly stretched its lead to 1 lap, but safety cars and pit cycles meant it was #7 Porsche leading after both cars had made their final stop. The gap closed up during a late safety car period, and #1 Audi fought back to take the lead on track, bringing it home to take the win

  18. Monterey Sports Car Championships
    Mazda Raceway Laguna Seca, Monterey, California
    Date: 20.10.2007
    Series: ALMS
    Race Format: 4 Hours
    Classes: P1, P2, GT1, GT2
    Circuit Length: 3.602 km
    Laps Completed: 157
    Distance Covered: 565.514 km
    Number of cars entered: 30 (7 P1, 9 P2, 2 GT1, 12 GT2)
    Number of cars finished: 23 (5 P1, 6 P2, 2 GT1, 10 GT2)
    Pole Position: #6 Penske Motorsports, Porsche RS Spyder Evo, Sascha Maassen(DEU), Ryan Briscoe(AUS), 1.10,528
    Overall Winner: #1 Audi Sport North America, Audi R10 TDI, Rinaldo Capello(ITA), Allan McNish(GBR), 4:00.14,224
    P2 Winner: #7 Penske Motorsports, Porsche RS Spyder Evo, Timo Bernhard(DEU), Romain Dumas(FRA), +0,410
    GT1 Winner: #4 Corvette Racing, Chevrolet Corvette C6.R, Oliver Gavin(GBR), Olivier Beretta(MCO), +7 Laps
    GT2 Winner: #62 Risi Competizione, Ferrari F430 GTC, Mika Salo(FIN), Jaime Melo(BRA), +11 Laps
    Porsche locked out the front row and led the start as both Acuras spun in T1. After a short safety car period #1 Audi put pressure on the leading Porsches, and eventually took the lead in traffic. The leaders made their first stop during another safety car later in the first hour, with the Porsches jumping ahead of the Audis as #2 was penalized for a pit stop infringement, and #15 Lola Acura stayed out and took the lead. On the restart #1 made a stunning launch to vault straight to the lead ahead of the two Porsches as #15 was swamped. Another safety car later in the 2nd hour saw the second round of pit stops, again the Porsches with the faster stops as #7 took the lead ahead of #1, and #6 jumped #2 until it slid off on the pit exit. #9 Acura was fighting back from its earlier delays, but suffered a puncture after contact with #2 Audi following a stern block, before it collided with #16 Dyson and went off and retired. The resulting safety car saw the third round of pit stops for the leaders, but with several cars staying out the Dysons cycled to the front split by #7 Porsche, with the Audis further back in the field. However the grunt of the Audi saw #1 cut through the field to take the lead, with #7 Porsche following it into 2nd. Another safety car in the final hour saw the leaders make their final stop, with #7 taking the lead ahead of #1. The power of the Audi meant #1 re-took the lead at the restart, however #7 Porsche maintained the pressure and they diced for the lead as darkness descended. However the Audi stayed cool and held on to take the win, with #2 finishing third after fighting back from earlier delays

2008 Season

Overview:

Audi expanded their program for the third season with the R10, competing in ALMS as well as in the LMS. Peugeot also continued for a full season in LMS, but they also joined ALMS at Sebring and Petit Le Mans.
Pescarolo continued into their 2nd season in the LMS with the 01, the car proving popular amongst customer teams as well, both in LMP1 and LMP2.
Porsche continued into their third season in the ALMS with the RS Spyder, with the factory team again focusing exclusively on North America. However some privateer teams brought the RS Spyder to Europe to compete in LMS and at Le Mans.
Following an encouraging first season Acura expanded their program for 2008, with 4 teams using the updated ARX-01b. AGR and Highcroft continue from 2007, with the Fernandez team returning now also with the Acura chassis after competing with a Lola the previous year. The 4th team to join the program was the newly created de Ferran motorsports.
Minor changes in the regulations for LMP1 and LMP2 announced by the ACO to further level the performance between petrol and diesel cars, as well as increasing the gap between LMP1 and LMP2. IMSA chose to implement some of these changes, primarily to slow the P2 cars, which dominated large parts of the previous season.
ALMS focused on continuity and revealed a calendar featuring all the events from 2007, with only small adjustments to race lengths.
Meanwhile LMS featured a modified calendar, with the event in Valencia moving to Barcelona, and the overseas round in Brazil removed.
After two dire seasons of the JLMC, with small grids and few interested teams, the series was cancelled after the ACO briefly took control of it, with the focus instead shifting to create a new series known as the Asian Le Mans Series, with an test event planned in Shanghai at the end of the year.

2023 Season

Overview:

3 years after the announcement of the convergence between the top class in IMSA and FIA/ACO, the new LMDh cars debuted in the GTP class. Acura and Cadillac built new cars based on their previous DPi cars, with Porsche and BMW joining with all new cars. Acura and BMW chose to compete in IMSA, while Porsche and Cadillac also joined the FIA WEC.
Ferrari also joined the WEC with a new LMH, along with the ByKolles Vanwall, which had finally sorted the legal issues with the Vanwall brand. After debuting half way through 2022, Peugeot started their first full season, with Toyota and Glickenhaus also continuing with similar programs to 2022.
Isotta Fraschini also launced a new LMH, but with a very short timeline, they were rejected from a full season entry.
With Porsche and Ferrari both focusing on their Hypercar/GTP programs, resulting in potentially only Corvette running in GTE-Pro, the FIA and ACO decided to end the class at the end of 2022, leaving only a single GTE class for 2023.
WEC started a gradual expansion after conservative seasons following COVID-19, keeping the races from 2022, and adding a race in Portugal, where they previously were in 2021, as well as announcing a new event in Qatar for 2024.
IMSA made a few changes to their calendar, with Mid-Ohio and Detroit dropping out, replaced by a new event at Indianapolis.

  2. Rolex 24 at Daytona
    Daytona International Speedway, Daytona Beach, Florida
    Date: 28-29.01.2023
    Series: IMSA
    Race Format: 24 Hours
    Classes: GTP, LMP2, LMP3, GTD Pro, GTD
    Circuit Length: 5.729 km
    Laps Completed: 783
    Distance Covered: 4485.807 km
    Number of cars entered: 61 (9 GTP, 10 LMP2, 9 LMP3, 10 GTD Pro, 23 GTD)
    Number of cars finished: 45 (8 GTP, 7 LMP2, 5 LMP3, 8 GTD Pro, 17 GTD)
    Pole Position: #60 Meyer Shank Racing, Acura ARX-06, Tom Blomqvist(GBR), Colin Braun(USA), Helio Castroneves(BRA), Simon Pagenaud(FRA), 1.34,031
    Overall Winner: #60 Meyer Shank Racing, Acura ARX-06, Tom Blomqvist(GBR), Colin Braun(USA), Helio Castroneves(BRA), Simon Pagenaud(FRA), 24:01.19,952
    LMP2 Winner: #55 Proton Competition, Oreca 07 - Gibson, Gianmaria Bruni(ITA), James Allen(AUS), Francesco Pizzi(ITA), Fred Poordad(USA), +22 Laps
    LMP3 Winner: #17 AWA, Duqueine D08 - Nissan, Wayne Boyd(GBR), Nicolas Varrone(ARG), Anthony Mantella(CAN), Thomas Merrill(USA), +46 Laps
    GTD Winner: #27 Heart of Racing Team, Aston Martin Vantage AMR GT3, Marco Sørensen(DEN), Darren Turner(GBR), Roman De Angelis(CAN), Ian James(GBR), +54 Laps
    GTD Pro Winner: #79 WeatherTech Racing, Mercedes-AMG GT3 Evo, Maro Engel(DEU), Jules Gounon(FRA), Daniel Juncadella(ESP), Cooper MacNeil(USA), +54 Laps
    #60 Acura led the early stages with the #25 BMW hitting trouble less than an hour in with a hybrid issue, spending several hours in the garage. #01 Cadillac briefly took the lead when the #60 Acura had to make several pit stops under a safety car period 2 hour in, changing the tail after suffering rear wing damage. However the Acura re-took the lead with a faster stop under another safety car an hour later. #7 Porsche also suffered a hybrid issue around the 6 hour mark, losing several laps changing the battery in the garage. Throughout the night the Acuras developed issues with the oil system, #10 requiring a short trip to the garage to replace the oil filter and oil filler cap. The #60 was having similar issues, having to make several pit stops to manage the issue while staying withing touching distance of the lead lap. As Sunday morning approached the #31 Cadillac slowed and went into the garage with broken suspension after contact, dropping several laps down. Soon after the remaining #6 Porsche spun off, suffering rear damage and dropping out of the lead battle as it pitted for repairs. Throughout Sunday morning the BMWs suffered more issues, #25 with a minor gearbox issue and #24 had brake issues requiring a visit to the garage. The #7 Porsche also suffered a broken water pipe, costing more laps. Drama as the #6 Porsche suffered a gearbox failure 3 hours from the end, stopping on track with smoke coming out of the rear, retiring after getting back to the pits on electric power. The fight for the win was mainly contested by the #60 Acura and the #01 and #02 Cadillacs, however with a series of safety cars in the closing hours, the #10 Acura went from 2 laps down to the lead lap, and it soon took the Cadillacs for 2nd, however the #60 Acura held on in the closing stages to take the win.

  3. 1000 Miles of Sebring
    Sebring International Raceway, Sebring, Florida
    Date: 17.03.2023
    Series: WEC
    Race Format: 1000 Miles or 8 Hours
    Classes: Hypercar, LMP2, LMGTE-Am
    Circuit Length: 6.019 km
    Laps Completed: 239
    Distance Covered: 1438.541 km
    Number of cars entered: 37 (11 Hypercar, 12 LMP2, 14 LMGTE-Am)
    Number of cars finished: 31 (9 Hypercar, 10 LMP2, 12 LMGTE-Am)
    Pole Position: #50 Ferrari AF Corse, Ferrari 499P, Antonio Fuoco(ITA), Miguel Molina(ESP), Nicklas Nielsen(DEN), 1.45,067
    Overall Winner: #7 Toyota Gazoo Racing, Toyota GR010 Hybrid, Mike Conway(GBR), Kamui Kobayashi(JAP), Jose Maria Lopez(ARG), 8:00.19,877
    LMP2 Winner: #48 Hertz Team Jota, Oreca 07 - Gibson, Yifei Ye(CHN), William Stevens(GBR), David Beckmann(DEU), +9 Laps
    LMGTE-Am Winner: #33 Corvette Racing, Chevrolet Corvette C8.R, Nicky Catsburg(NED), Nicolas Varrone(ARG), Ben Keating(USA), +18 Laps
    #50 Ferrari led from Pole as #94 Peugeot suffered a gearbox failure on the formation lap and went straight to the garage. An early SC saw the two Ferraris pit for fuel, leaving the Toyotas in the lead. On the restart #708 Glickenhaus stopped on track with electrical issues, eventually getting going again. 1h into the race #93 Peugeot also suffered a gearbox failure and dropped down the order as it went to the garage. As the leaders made their first stop the Ferraris briefly cycled back to the front until they made their 2nd stop. The battle for 3rd towards the end of the 2nd stint was fierce between #6 Porsche and #2 Cadillac, the Porsche struggling on worn tyres. #94 suffered a hybrid issue and pulled into the garage and retired. #7 Toyota led until the 2nd stop, where #8 stayed out 2 more laps and came out ahead. #708 suffered more electrical issues and stopped on track, retiring from the race. Contact between #93 Peugeot and #4 Vanwall near the 3h mark as the FCY came out, #93 spinning and #4 having to pit with bodywork damage. As another FCY came out #8 Toyota was about to pit from the lead, but could only take emergency fuel as the pits were closed, having to come in again when the race went back to green, however it kept the lead. However it later lost the lead as it was saving fuel, dropping behind #7. Drama at the 6h mark as #51 Ferrari had contact in traffic, crashing out and suffering a puncture and substantial rear damage, dropping several laps down while in the garage. Vanwall had a steady race, until a suspension failure in the 7th hour, it too spending time in the garage fixing the damage.
    #7 cruised home to take the win ahead of sister #8, with #50 finishing 3rd

  4. Mobil 1 Twelve Hours of Sebring
    Sebring International Raceway, Sebring, Florida
    Date: 18.03.2023
    Series: IMSA
    Race Format: 12 Hours
    Classes: GTP, LMP2, LMP3, GTD Pro, GTD
    Circuit Length: 6.019 km
    Laps Completed: 322
    Distance Covered: 1938.118 km
    Number of cars entered: 54 (8 GTP, 8 LMP2, 10 LMP3, 8 GTD Pro, 20 GTD)
    Number of cars finished: 39 (3 GTP, 6 LMP2, 7 LMP3, 8 GTD Pro, 15 GTD)
    Pole Position: #31 Action Express Racing, Cadillac V-Series.R, Luis Felipe Derani(BRA), Alexander Sims(GBR), Jack Aitken(GBR), 1.45,836
    Overall Winner: #31 Action Express Racing, Cadillac V-Series.R, Luis Felipe Derani(BRA), Alexander Sims(GBR), Jack Aitken(GBR), 12:00.53,382
    LMP2 Winner: #8 Tower Motorsports, Oreca 07 - Gibson, Kyffin Simpson(BAR), Scott McLaughlin(NZE), John Farano(CAN), +4 Laps
    LMP3 Winner: #74 Riley Motorsports, Ligier JS P320 - Nissan, Felipe Fraga(BRA), Josh Burdon(AUS), Gar Robinson(USA), +13 Laps
    GTD Pro Winner: #9 Pfaff Motorsports, Porsche 911 GT3 R (992), Klaus Bachler(AUT), Patrick Pilet(FRA), Laurens Vanthoor(BEL), +19 Laps
    GTD Winner: #1 Paul Miller Racing, BMW M4 GT3, Corey Lewis(USA), Bryan Sellers(USA), Madison Snow(USA), +21 Laps
    #31 Cadillac led the opening stages as #01 Cadillac and #10 Acura traded places in the first stint, before #01 took the lead at the first stop. A safety car restart during the 2nd stint saw #31 struggle on old tyres, dropping down the order until it had contact with a spinning car and then scattering debris everywhere trying to stay out before being forced to come in. When the leaders pitted #10 took the lead, but trying to double stint tyres it dropped down the order leaving #01 back in front. #6 Porsche suffered early issues, first diagnosing a hydraulic issue under the safety car, and then a puncture 3h in cost it time. During the 4th hour #24 BMW went off and suffered damage, and #6 slowed on track with fumes in the cockpit, as #7 Porsche suffered suspension issues and pitted for repairs. #01 had built a substantial lead, but a safety car at the 5h mark wiped it out with #10 taking the lead after pitting just before, with the rest stopping when the pit lane opened. #31 made it back to the lead lap, and traded places multiple times with #01 for 2nd overall until another SC, at which point #24 BMW stopped on track and retired with overheating. After the restart #01 struggled on old tyres and dropped from 2nd to 7th, as a bizarre incident under SC at the 7h mark saw an LMP3 car unlapping itself hit the rear of #6, both cars suffering damage. #31 took the lead as the leaders cycled through the pits, with #10 penalized for speeding. After a safety car during the 9th hour #01 muscled its way into the lead, with #10 following it into 2nd, dropping #31 to 3rd, however at the 9h mark #01 pitted from the lead and retired with engine failure. More drama with less than 2h to go as #60 Acura lost a wheel and stopped on track. The leaders pitted in anticipation of the SC, leaving #25 in the lead until it stopped when the pits opened and changed the brakes, with #6 taking tyres. On the restart #6 Porsche on new tyres took 3rd from #31, and after another SC restart with 1h to go it took 2nd from #7, pressuring #10 for the lead, banging wheels. #31 made its final stop, with #7 pitting to serve a penalty for a pit stop infringement as another SC came out. When the pits opened #10 and #6 made their final stop, with #7 also pitting for new tyres. On the restart #6 again went aggressive and took the lead, with #31 shuffled from the lead to 4th, until with 18 min to go #6 was baulked in traffic, contact with #10 ending in both cars crashing out, #7 failing to avoid it with all three cars eliminated.
    That left #31 leading ahead of #25, and they controlled the pace as the race restarted with 5min left to take the win

  5. Acura Grand Prix of Long Beach
    Long Beach Street Circuit, Long Beach, California
    Date: 15.04.2023
    Series: IMSA
    Race Format: 1 Hour 40 minutes
    Classes: GTP, GTD Pro, GTD
    Circuit Length: 3.167 km
    Laps Completed: 78
    Distance Covered: 247.026 km
    Number of cars entered: 28 (8 GTP, 5 GTD Pro, 15 GTD)
    Number of cars finished: 24 (6 GTP, 5 GTD Pro, 13 GTD)
    Pole Position: #10 Wayne Taylor Racing, Acura ARX-06, Ricky Taylor(USA), Felipe Albuquerque(POR), 1.09,909
    Overall Winner: #6 Porsche Penske Motorsports, Porsche 963, Mathieu Jaminet(FRA), Nick Tandy(GBR), 1:42.08,126
    GTD Pro Winner: #14 Vasser Sullivan Racing, Lexus RC F GT3, Ben Barnicoat(GBR), Jack Hawksworth(GBR), +5 Laps
    GTD Winner: #1 Paul Miller Racing, BMW M4 GT3, Bryan Sellers(USA), Madison Snow(USA), +5 Laps
    The two Acuras locked out the front row, as #01 Cadillac spun and crashed at the start, with #60 Acura also spinning after contact with #25 BMW
    #10 Acura led the early stages ahead of #6 Porsche and the two BMWs. #31 Cadillac made a very early stop just 15 min in, dropping almost a lap down
    As the leaders made their only stop of the race, #10 went from the lead to 5th after being delayed at its stop, with the Porsches ending up 1st and 3rd after not taking tyres
    #31 Cadillac pitted from 2nd for its 2nd stop with 30 min to go, leaving #7 Porsche 2nd under massive pressure on old tyres, first from #25 BMW until it went off, then the #10 Acura
    After enormous pressure #10 Acura took 2nd, with #25 following it through having also re-joined the battle with the #7
    #10 quickly caught the leading #6 and tried to take the lead with just 2 laps to go, but braked too late and crashed out, leaving #6 Porsche to take the win

  6. 6 Hours of Portimao
    Algarve International Circuit, Portimao, Portugal
    Date: 16.04.2023
    Series: WEC
    Race Format: 6 Hours
    Classes: Hypercar, LMP2, LMGTE-Am
    Circuit Length: 4.653 km
    Laps Completed: 222
    Distance Covered: 1032.966 km
    Number of cars entered: 37 (11 Hypercar, 12 LMP2, 14 LMGTE-Am)
    Number of cars finished: 35 (10 Hypercar, 12 LMP2, 13 LMGTE-Am)
    Pole Position: #8 Toyota Gazoo Racing, Toyota GR010 Hybrid, Sebastien Buemi(CHF), Brendon Hartley(NZE), Ryo Hirakawa(JAP), 1.30,171
    Overall Winner: #8 Toyota Gazoo Racing, Toyota GR010 Hybrid, Sebastien Buemi(CHF), Brendon Hartley(NZE), Ryo Hirakawa(JAP), 6:01.26,343
    LMP2 Winner: #23 United Autosports, Oreca 07 - Gibson, Giedo van der Garde(NED), Oliver Jarvis(GBR), Josh Pierson(USA), +7 Laps
    LMGTE-Am Winner: #33 Corvette Racing, Chevrolet Corvette C8.R, Nicky Catsburg(NED), Nicolas Varrone(ARG), Ben Keating(USA), +16 Laps
    Toyota locked out the front row, with #7 taking an early lead and #51 Ferrari briefly in 2nd until #8 re-took the place. #93 Peugeot started from the pit lane after having to change the steering column before the race. The two Ferraris argued over track position in the first stint, with #50 eventually getting ahead, with the two Toyotas too swapping places before the end of the first stint. As the cars cycled through the first stops, both #6 Porsche and #2 Cadillac jumped the two ferraris by not taking tyres, however both cars struggled in the second stint, with #2 having to stop again after suffering with a flat spot. Drama in the 2nd hour as #7 Toyota pitted from 2nd with a problem with a driveshaft torque sensor, the team forced to stop and change the parts, losing 7 laps. Problems also hit #51 Ferrari in the 3rd hour, suffering problems with the front braking system and having to make an extra stop to help the brake cooling. #5 Porsche slowed on track and pitted at the 4h mark, but after rejoining seemingly without problems it came back in shortly after with a power steering failure and dropped out of contention. #4 Vanwall suffered a brake failure and crashed out just before the 5h mark, bringing out the safety car. In the final hour #51 suffered a brake failure too, and slowed dramatically to nurse the car to the end. #6 Porsche looked set for 3rd place until it had to make a late splash of fuel to make it to the end, however it managed to hang on to finish ahead of the #2 Cadillac which finished 4th after running off sequence since the tyre issues earlier in the race.
    Meanwhile #8 Toyota went unchallenged to take the win ahead of the #50 Ferrari

  7. TotalEnergies 6 Hours of Spa-Franchorchamps
    Circuit de Spa-Franchorchamps, Stavelot, Belgium
    Date: 29.04.2023
    Series: WEC
    Race Format: 6 Hours
    Classes: Hypercar, LMP2, LMGTE-Am
    Circuit Length: 7.004 km
    Laps Completed: 148
    Distance Covered: 1036.592 km
    Number of cars entered: 38 (13 Hypercar, 11 LMP2, 14 LMGTE-Am)
    Number of cars finished: 31 (9 Hypercar, 10 LMP2, 12 LMGTE-Am)
    Pole Position: #7 Toyota Gazoo Racing, Toyota GR010 Hybrid, Mike Conway(GBR), Kamui Kobayashi(JAP), Jose Maria Lopez(ARG), 2.00,812
    Overall Winner: #7 Toyota Gazoo Racing, Toyota GR010 Hybrid, Mike Conway(GBR), Kamui Kobayashi(JAP), Jose Maria Lopez(ARG), 6:00.24,798
    LMP2 Winner: #41 Team WRT, Oreca 07 - Gibson, Robert Kubica(POL), Louis Deletraz(CHF), Rui Andrade(ANG), +2 Laps
    LMGTE-Am Winner: #83 Richard Mille AF Corse, Ferrari 488 GTE Evo, Alessio Rovera(ITA), Lilou Wadoux(FRA), Luis Perez Companc(ARG), +8 Laps
    The race started in damp and cold conditions, with half the cars starting on slicks and half on wets. After multiple spins and cars struggling to keep pace with the safety car an extra formation lap was added. #7 Toyota started on pole, but fell back on slicks along with #3 Cadillac and the Porsches. The wet-shod two Ferraris led the early stages ahead of #2 Cadillac, until an early safety car, at which point the track had dried enough that the slick runners could catch back up. #7 Toyota re-took the lead followed by #6 Porsche as the wet runners all pitted. Once on slicks, the two Ferraris struggled heavily to get up to temperature, haemorrhaging time and going a lap down. #5 Porsche and #8 Toyota gradually made their way towards the front, #8 having started at the back after an accident in qualifying. #6 Porsche lost time during the first pit cycle, falling behind #3 Cadillac and #8 Toyota as #7 maintained the lead, however #8 suffering on worn tyres fell back behind #6. Drama in the 2nd hour as #3 Cadillac suffered a heavy accident after a power steering failure, the car retiring with the driver sent to the medical centre. #6 Porsche was holding a strong 2nd place until a complete electrical failure saw the car stop on track and retire, as at the same time #4 Vanwall went off and got stuck in the gravel. Problems continued for #4 Vanwall, after briefly stopping on track before driving back slowly to close the door in the 4th hour, it got tangled up in traffic and crashed out of the race. After pitting in the 5th hout #50 Ferrari exited the pit lane and immediately crashed out on cold tyres, it too retiring from the race. #7 Toyota controlled the lead through the final stints despite late pressure from sister #8, including a 5 second penalty for overtaking off the track. #5 Porsche was set for 3rd place until #51 Ferrari hunted it down and took the place on the final lap
